    <li> This works well, but there is an equivalent on Amazon that works even better -- in kitchenware, the Microplane grater 40020.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;There are two reasons why it is better -- first, the kiitchen device is sharper (at least, mine is) and sharper tools require less effort and are easier to control; second, the Microplane kitchen device works on the pull stroke rather than the push stroke that the pedicure rasp uses. This is important -- on the pull stroke it keeps the rasp attached to the skin and is more controllable than in push mode. That&#x27;s why Japanese hand saws cut much more precisely with more control with the pull stroke than western saws that cut on the push stroke.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;So, for a few dollars more, get the better device from kitchenware.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;EDIT: After further use, I can see that the rasp is designed to work on the pull stroke as well as the push stroke because the \\&quot;teeth\\&quot; are set up with half facing each direction. However, I still say that the kitchen version works better, and maybe that is because all of the teeth work in the pull direction and the pull direction is the most useful.</li>
